**Use case:** Virtual DOM React-‡¶è fast ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç efficient rendering ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶ö‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§


‚úÖ 6. Forms & Events
### _#43._ üü£ **How do you handle forms in React?**

React-‡¶è forms handle ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶¶‡ßÅ‡¶ü‡¶ø approach ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º: **controlled components** ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç **uncontrolled components**‡•§ ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶ó ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßá‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá controlled components ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶æ React-‡¶è‡¶∞ state-driven philosophy-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá consistent‡•§

**Handling Forms (Controlled):**
- **State Management:** Form inputs-‡¶è‡¶∞ value state-‡¶è store ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç `onChange` ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá update ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
- **Event Handling:** `onSubmit` event ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá form submission handle ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
- **Validation:** State-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá validation logic apply ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§

**Example:**
```jsx
import { useState } from 'react';

const MyForm = () => {
  const [formData, setFormData] = useState({ name: '', email: '' });

  const handleChange = (e) => {
    const { name, value } = e.target;
    setFormData({ ...formData, [name]: value });
  };

  const handleSubmit = (e) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    console.log('Form submitted:', formData);
  };

  return (
    <form onSubmit={handleSubmit}>
      <input name="name" value={formData.name} onChange={handleChange} />
      <input name="email" value={formData.email} onChange={handleChange} />
      <button type="submit">Submit</button>
    </form>
  );
};
```

**Uncontrolled Approach:**
- `useRef` ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá input values access ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
- Less common, simple forms-‡¶è ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
```jsx
import { useRef } from 'react';

const MyForm = () => {
  const nameRef = useRef(null);

  const handleSubmit = (e) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    console.log('Name:', nameRef.current.value);
  };

  return (
    <form onSubmit={handleSubmit}>
      <input ref={nameRef} />
      <button type="submit">Submit</button>
    </form>
  );
};
```

**Use case:** Controlled forms ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶ø dynamic forms, validation, ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç state-driven apps-‡¶è‡•§ Uncontrolled forms simple, one-off forms-‡¶è‡•§



### _#44._ üü£ **What is a controlled component?**

Controlled component ‡¶π‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø React component ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá form input-‡¶è‡¶∞ value React state-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶Æ‡ßá control ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§ Input-‡¶è‡¶∞ value ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç changes state-‡¶è sync ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá‡•§

**Key Points:**
- Input-‡¶è‡¶∞ `value` prop state ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡ßá‡•§
- `onChange` event ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá state update ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
- React fully controls input-‡¶è‡¶∞ behavior‡•§

**Example:**
```jsx
import { useState } from 'react';

const ControlledInput = () => {
  const [value, setValue] = useState('');

  return (
    <input
      value={value}
      onChange={(e) => setValue(e.target.value)}
      placeholder="Enter text"
    />
  );
};
```

**Advantages:**
- State-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá input sync ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá‡•§
- Validation ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç dynamic updates ‡¶∏‡¶π‡¶ú‡•§
- Form data manipulate ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§

**Use case:** Controlled components ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶ø complex forms, real-time validation, ‡¶¨‡¶æ state-dependent UI-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø‡•§



### _#45._ üü£ **What is event handling in React and how is it different from HTML?**

**Event Handling in React:**
React-‡¶è event handling ‡¶π‡¶≤‡ßã user interactions (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® click, input change, submit) handle ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø synthetic events ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡•§ React events camelCase-‡¶è ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç event handlers JSX-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶Æ‡ßá components-‡¶è attach ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§

**Example:**
```jsx
const Button = () => {
  const handleClick = (event) => {
    console.log('Clicked:', event.target);
  };

  return <button onClick={handleClick}>Click me</button>;
};
```

**Differences from HTML:**

| **Aspect**             | **React**                                                    | **HTML**                                                   |
|------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------|
| **Event Names**        | camelCase (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® `onClick`, `onChange`)                      | lowercase (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® `onclick`, `onchange`)                    |
| **Event System**       | Synthetic events, React-‡¶è‡¶∞ wrapper                           | Native browser events                                     |
| **Event Handler**      | Functions passed as props (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® `onClick={handleClick}`)    | Inline strings (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® `onclick="handleClick()"`)           |
| **Event Object**       | SyntheticEvent, cross-browser compatible                     | Native event object, browser-specific                     |
| **Performance**        | Event delegation ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá performance optimize ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá               | Direct event listeners, less optimized                    |
| **Prevent Default**    | `e.preventDefault()`                                        | `return false` ‡¶¨‡¶æ `event.preventDefault()`                |

**Example (React vs HTML):**
```jsx
// React
<button onClick={(e) => console.log(e)}>Click</button>

// HTML
<button onclick="console.log(event)">Click</button>
```

**Use case:** React-‡¶è‡¶∞ event handling cross-browser consistency ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç performance optimization-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§



### _#46._ üü£ **How do you handle input validation in forms?**

React-‡¶è form input validation ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º:

1. **State-Based Validation:**
   - Input state-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá validation logic apply ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡•§
   - Error messages state-‡¶è store ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá conditionally render ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡•§

**Example:**
```jsx
import { useState } from 'react';

const MyForm = () => {
  const [formData, setFormData] = useState({ email: '', password: '' });
  const [errors, setErrors] = useState({ email: '', password: '' });

  const validate = () => {
    let valid = true;
    const newErrors = { email: '', password: '' };

    if (!formData.email.includes('@')) {
      newErrors.email = 'Invalid email';
      valid = false;
    }
    if (formData.password.length < 6) {
      newErrors.password = 'Password must be at least 6 characters';
      valid = false;
    }

    setErrors(newErrors);
    return valid;
  };

  const handleChange = (e) => {
    const { name, value } = e.target;
    setFormData({ ...formData, [name]: value });
  };

  const handleSubmit = (e) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    if (validate()) {
      console.log('Form submitted:', formData);
    }
  };

  return (
    <form onSubmit={handleSubmit}>
      <div>
        <input
          name="email"
          value={formData.email}
          onChange={handleChange}
          placeholder="Email"
        />
        {errors.email && <p>{errors.email}</p>}
      </div>
      <div>
        <input
          name="password"
          value={formData.password}
          onChange={handleChange}
          type="password"
          placeholder="Password"
        />
        {errors.password && <p>{errors.password}</p>}
      </div>
      <button type="submit">Submit</button>
    </form>
  );
};
```

2. **Third-Party Libraries:**
   - **Formik:** Form handling ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç validation ‡¶∏‡¶π‡¶ú ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
   - **Yup:** Schema-based validation Formik-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
   ```jsx
   import { Formik, Form, Field } from 'formik';
   import * as Yup from 'yup';

   const validationSchema = Yup.object({
     email: Yup.string().email('Invalid email').required('Required'),
     password: Yup.string().min(6, 'Minimum 6 characters').required('Required'),
   });

   const MyForm = () => (
     <Formik
       initialValues={{ email: '', password: '' }}
       validationSchema={validationSchema}
       onSubmit={(values) => console.log(values)}
     >
       {({ errors, touched }) => (
         <Form>
           <Field name="email" />
           {touched.email && errors.email && <p>{errors.email}</p>}
           <Field name="password" type="password" />
           {touched.password && errors.password && <p>{errors.password}</p>}
           <button type="submit">Submit</button>
         </Form>
       )}
     </Formik>
   );
   ```

3. **Real-Time Validation:**
   - `onChange` ‡¶¨‡¶æ `onBlur` event-‡¶è validation trigger ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡•§
   - Debouncing ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá frequent validation calls ‡¶ï‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã‡•§

4. **Server-Side Validation:**
   - Form submission-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞ API ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá errors ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶®‡ßá display ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡•§

**Use case:** Input validation ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶ø user input ‡¶∏‡¶†‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶æ check ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç user-friendly error messages ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá‡•§


‚úÖ 7. Routing, State Management, and Tools
### _#47._ üü£ **What is React Router and how does it work?**

React Router ‡¶π‡¶≤‡ßã React-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ú‡¶®‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º routing library ‡¶Ø‡¶æ single-page applications (SPAs)-‡¶è client-side navigation handle ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§ ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶æ URL-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá components render ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç page refresh ‡¶õ‡¶æ‡¶°‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶á navigation ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶¨ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§

**How it works:**
- **BrowserRouter:** HTML5 history API ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá routing manage ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
- **Routes & Route:** URL path-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá components map ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
- **Link/NavLink:** Navigation-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø `<a>`-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º, ‡¶Ø‡¶æ page reload prevent ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
- **Dynamic Routing:** URL parameters (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® `:id`) ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá dynamic content render ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§

**Example:**
```jsx
import { BrowserRouter, Routes, Route, Link } from 'react-router-dom';

const Home = () => <h1>Home</h1>;
const About = () => <h1>About</h1>;

const App = () => (
  <BrowserRouter>
    <nav>
      <Link to="/">Home</Link> | <Link to="/about">About</Link>
    </nav>
    <Routes>
      <Route path="/" element={<Home />} />
      <Route path="/about" element={<About />} />
    </Routes>
  </BrowserRouter>
);
```

**Use case:** React Router ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶ø SPA-‡¶§‡ßá multiple views ‡¶¨‡¶æ pages (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® Home, Profile) manage ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá‡•§



### _#48._ üü£ **What are nested routes?**

Nested routes ‡¶π‡¶≤‡ßã React Router-‡¶è ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶™‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø route-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∞‡ßã sub-routes define ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§ ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶æ hierarchical UI structure ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá, ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá parent route-‡¶è‡¶∞ component child routes-‡¶è‡¶∞ components render ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§

**How it works:**
- Parent route-‡¶è `<Outlet />` component ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º, ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá child routes render ‡¶π‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§
- URL structure nested paths reflect ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§

**Example:**
```jsx
import { BrowserRouter, Routes, Route, Link, Outlet } from 'react-router-dom';

const App = () => (
  <BrowserRouter>
    <Routes>
      <Route path="/" element={<Layout />}>
        <Route index element={<Home />} />
        <Route path="profile" element={<Profile />}>
          <Route path="settings" element={<Settings />} />
          <Route path="details" element={<Details />} />
        </Route>
      </Route>
    </Routes>
  </BrowserRouter>
);

const Layout = () => (
  <div>
    <nav>
      <Link to="/">Home</Link> | <Link to="/profile">Profile</Link> | 
      <Link to="/profile/settings">Settings</Link> | <Link to="/profile/details">Details</Link>
    </nav>
    <Outlet /> {/* Child routes render here */}
  </div>
);

const Home = () => <h1>Home</h1>;
const Profile = () => <div><h1>Profile</h1><Outlet /></div>;
const Settings = () => <h1>Settings</h1>;
const Details = () => <h1>Details</h1>;
```

**Use case:** Nested routes ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶ø complex layouts (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® dashboard-‡¶è sidebar + sub-pages) ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá‡•§



### _#49._ üü£ **What is Redux and how does it work with React?**

Redux ‡¶π‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø open-source JavaScript library ‡¶Ø‡¶æ predictable state management-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§ React-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá Redux global state manage ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º, ‡¶Ø‡¶æ multiple components-‡¶è share ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§

**How it works:**
- **Store:** Single source of truth, ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá app-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶¨ state store ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
- **Actions:** State change-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø payloads (objects) ‡¶Ø‡¶æ dispatch ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
- **Reducers:** Pure functions ‡¶Ø‡¶æ actions-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá state update ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
- **React-Redux:** `Provider` ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç `useSelector`/`useDispatch` hooks ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá Redux store-‡¶ï‡ßá React-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá connect ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§

**Example:**
```jsx
import { createStore } from 'redux';
import { Provider, useSelector, useDispatch } from 'react-redux';

// Reducer
const counterReducer = (state = { count: 0 }, action) => {
  switch (action.type) {
    case 'INCREMENT': return { count: state.count + 1 };
    case 'DECREMENT': return { count: state.count - 1 };
    default: return state;
  }
};

// Store
const store = createStore(counterReducer);

// Component
const Counter = () => {
  const count = useSelector((state) => state.count);
  const dispatch = useDispatch();

  return (
    <div>
      <p>Count: {count}</p>
      <button onClick={() => dispatch({ type: 'INCREMENT' })}>Increment</button>
      <button onClick={() => dispatch({ type: 'DECREMENT' })}>Decrement</button>
    </div>
  );
};

// App
const App = () => (
  <Provider store={store}>
    <Counter />
  </Provider>
);
```

**Use case:** Redux ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶ø large-scale apps-‡¶è complex state (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® user data, app settings) manage ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá‡•§



### _#50._ üü£ **What is the difference between Redux and Context API?**

| **Aspect**              | **Redux**                                                  | **Context API**                                            |
|-------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------|
| **Purpose**             | Large-scale state management library                      | Built-in React feature for sharing data across components |
| **Setup Complexity**    | More boilerplate (store, actions, reducers)               | Simpler setup (createContext, Provider)                   |
| **Scalability**         | Highly scalable, complex apps-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø                    | Small to medium apps-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø                             |
| **Performance**         | Optimized, middleware support ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá                        | Less optimized, frequent updates re-renders trigger ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá |
| **Tooling**             | DevTools, middleware (thunk, saga)                       | No built-in dev tools                                    |
| **State Logic**         | Centralized (store, reducers)                            | Decentralized (multiple contexts)                        |
| **Use Case**            | Complex state, frequent updates                          | Simple state sharing (theme, auth)                       |

**Example (Context API):**
```jsx
const ThemeContext = createContext();

const App = () => {
  const [theme, setTheme] = useState('light');
  return (
    <ThemeContext.Provider value={{ theme, setTheme }}>
      <Child />
    </ThemeContext.Provider>
  );
};

const Child = () => {
  const { theme } = useContext(ThemeContext);
  return <div>Theme: {theme}</div>;
};
```

**Use case:** Redux large apps-‡¶è complex state-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø, Context API simple state sharing-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø‡•§



### _#51._ üü£ **What are actions, reducers, and the store in Redux?**

1. **Actions:**
   - Objects ‡¶Ø‡¶æ state change-‡¶è‡¶∞ intention ‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶£‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
   - `type` property ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶§‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶π‡¶¨‡ßá; optional payload ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
   - `dispatch` ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá store-‡¶è ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
   ```jsx
   const increment = { type: 'INCREMENT' };
   const addTodo = { type: 'ADD_TODO', payload: 'Learn Redux' };
   ```

2. **Reducers:**
   - Pure functions ‡¶Ø‡¶æ current state ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç action ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá new state return ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
   - State immutable ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá, ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶á spread operator ‡¶¨‡¶æ new object ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
   ```jsx
   const counterReducer = (state = { count: 0 }, action) => {
     switch (action.type) {
       case 'INCREMENT': return { count: state.count + 1 };
       default: return state;
     }
   };
   ```

3. **Store:**
   - Single source of truth, ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá app-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶¨ state store ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
   - `createStore` ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
   - Methods: `getState`, `dispatch`, `subscribe`‡•§
   ```jsx
   import { createStore } from 'redux';
   const store = createStore(counterReducer);
   ```

**Use case:** Actions state changes trigger ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá, reducers state update ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá, ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç store ‡¶∏‡¶¨‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ centralized ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ñ‡ßá‡•§



### _#52._ üü£ **What is middleware in Redux?**

Middleware ‡¶π‡¶≤‡ßã Redux-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø extension point ‡¶Ø‡¶æ action dispatch ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç reducer-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ù‡ßá custom logic (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® logging, async operations) execute ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§

**How it works:**
- Middleware action intercept ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç side effects (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® API calls) handle ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
- `applyMiddleware` ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá store-‡¶è middleware add ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
- Popular middleware: `redux-thunk`, `redux-saga`, `redux-logger`‡•§

**Example (redux-thunk):**
```jsx
import { createStore, applyMiddleware } from 'redux';
import thunk from 'redux-thunk';

const fetchData = () => async (dispatch) => {
  const response = await fetch('https://api.example.com/data');
  const data = await response.json();
  dispatch({ type: 'FETCH_SUCCESS', payload: data });
};

const store = createStore(reducer, applyMiddleware(thunk));

// Component
const MyComponent = () => {
  const dispatch = useDispatch();
  return <button onClick={() => dispatch(fetchData())}>Fetch</button>;
};
```

**Use case:** Middleware ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶ø async operations, logging, ‡¶¨‡¶æ action transformation-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø‡•§



### _#53._ üü£ **What are some alternatives to Redux? (e.g., Zustand, Recoil)**

Redux-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º alternatives:

1. **Zustand:**
   - Lightweight state management library‡•§
   - Minimal API, no boilerplate‡•§
   - Hooks-based, simple store creation‡•§
   **Example:**
   ```jsx
   import create from 'zustand';

   const useStore = create((set) => ({
     count: 0,
     increment: () => set((state) => ({ count: state.count + 1 })),
   }));

   const Counter = () => {
     const { count, increment } = useStore();
     return <button onClick={increment}>{count}</button>;
   };
   ```
   **Use case:** Small to medium apps-‡¶è simple state management‡•§

2. **Recoil:**
   - Facebook-‡¶è‡¶∞ state management library‡•§
   - Atom ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç selector-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶Æ‡ßá granular state management‡•§
   - React-‡¶è‡¶∞ concurrent features-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá compatible‡•§
   **Example:**
   ```jsx
   import { atom, useRecoilState } from 'recoil';

   const countState = atom({
     key: 'countState',
     default: 0,
   });

   const Counter = () => {
     const [count, setCount] = useRecoilState(countState);
     return <button onClick={() => setCount(count + 1)}>{count}</button>;
   };
   ```
   **Use case:** Complex apps-‡¶è fine-grained state management‡•§

3. **Context API + useReducer:**
   - Built-in React solution‡•§
   - Simple apps-‡¶è Redux-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
   **Use case:** Lightweight apps-‡¶è global state‡•§

4. **MobX:**
   - Reactive state management‡•§
   - Observables ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá automatic updates‡•§
   **Use case:** Apps ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá reactive programming ‡¶™‡¶õ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶¶‡•§

**Comparison:**
- **Zustand:** Simple, minimal, fast‡•§
- **Recoil:** Modern, granular, React-focused‡•§
- **Context API:** No external dependency, limited scalability‡•§
- **MobX:** Reactive, less predictable than Redux‡•§

**Use case:** Alternatives ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶ø app size ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç complexity-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶â‡¶™‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§



‚úÖ 8. Testing & Best Practices
### _#54._ üü£ **How do you test a React component?**

React components-‡¶ï‡ßá test ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ **unit testing** ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç **integration testing** ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§ React Testing Library ‡¶¨‡¶æ Jest-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶§‡ßã tools ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá components-‡¶è‡¶∞ behavior, rendering, ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç user interactions test ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§

**Steps to Test a React Component:**
1. **Setup Testing Environment:**
   - Jest (test runner) ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç React Testing Library install ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
   - `npm install --save-dev @testing-library/react jest`.
2. **Write Test Cases:**
   - Render component-‡¶è‡¶∞ output test ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
   - User events (click, input) simulate ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
   - State changes ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç props handling verify ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
3. **Run Tests:** `npm test` ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá tests execute ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§

**Example:**
```jsx
// MyComponent.jsx
import { useState } from 'react';

const MyComponent = () => {
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0);
  return (
    <div>
      <p data-testid="count">Count: {count}</p>
      <button onClick={() => setCount(count + 1)}>Increment</button>
    </div>
  );
};

// MyComponent.test.jsx
import { render, screen, fireEvent } from '@testing-library/react';
import MyComponent from './MyComponent';

test('renders count and increments on button click', () => {
  render(<MyComponent />);
  
  // Check initial render
  expect(screen.getByTestId('count')).toHaveTextContent('Count: 0');
  
  // Simulate button click
  fireEvent.click(screen.getByText('Increment'));
  
  // Check updated count
  expect(screen.getByTestId('count')).toHaveTextContent('Count: 1');
});
```

**Tools Used:**
- **Jest:** Test runner ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç assertion library‡•§
- **React Testing Library:** Component rendering ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç interaction testing‡•§
- **Enzyme** (optional): Older alternative for shallow rendering‡•§
- **@testing-library/user-event:** Advanced user interactions (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® typing)‡•§

**Use case:** Component testing ensure ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡ßá UI ‡¶∏‡¶†‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá render ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç user interactions expected behavior ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶¶‡¶æ‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§



### _#55._ üü£ **What is the difference between unit testing and integration testing?**

| **Aspect**              | **Unit Testing**                                          | **Integration Testing**                                  |
|-------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------|---------------------------------------------------------|
| **Definition**          | Individual components ‡¶¨‡¶æ functions-‡¶è‡¶∞ isolated testing‡•§  | Multiple components ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßÄ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ test ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡•§ |
| **Scope**               | Single function, component, ‡¶¨‡¶æ module‡•§                   | Multiple components, APIs, ‡¶¨‡¶æ systems-‡¶è‡¶∞ interaction‡•§  |
| **Focus**               | Specific logic ‡¶¨‡¶æ behavior‡•§                              | Components-‡¶è‡¶∞ integration ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç data flow‡•§               |
| **Example**             | Button click-‡¶è state update test ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡•§                   | Form submission-‡¶è API call ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç UI update test ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡•§     |
| **Tools**               | Jest, React Testing Library (for components)‡•§            | Jest, React Testing Library, Cypress (end-to-end)‡•§     |
| **Complexity**          | Simpler, faster‡•§                                         | More complex, slower‡•§                                   |
| **Dependencies**        | Mocked/stubbed (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® API calls)‡•§                        | Real dependencies ‡¶¨‡¶æ partial mocks‡•§                     |

**Unit Testing Example:**
```jsx
test('increments count', () => {
  const { getByText } = render(<MyComponent />);
  fireEvent.click(getByText('Increment'));
  expect(getByTestId('count')).toHaveTextContent('Count: 1');
});
```

**Integration Testing Example:**
```jsx
test('form submits data to API', async () => {
  const mockApi = jest.fn().mockResolvedValue({ success: true });
  render(<Form api={mockApi} />);
  fireEvent.change(screen.getByLabelText('Name'), { target: { value: 'Alice' } });
  fireEvent.click(screen.getByText('Submit'));
  expect(mockApi).toHaveBeenCalledWith({ name: 'Alice' });
});
```

**Use case:** Unit testing individual components-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø, integration testing app-‡¶è‡¶∞ flow ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç interactions verify ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá‡•§



### _#56._ üü£ **What is React Testing Library and why is it popular?**

React Testing Library ‡¶π‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø lightweight testing library ‡¶Ø‡¶æ React components-‡¶è‡¶∞ testing-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø design ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá‡¶õ‡ßá‡•§ ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶æ user-centric testing encourage ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá, ‡¶Ö‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶•‡¶æ‡ßé ‡¶ï‡ßÄ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá users UI-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá interact ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ test ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§

**Key Features:**
- **DOM Testing:** Components render ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç DOM queries (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® `getByText`, `getByTestId`) ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶¶‡¶æ‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
- **User Interactions:** `fireEvent` ‡¶¨‡¶æ `@testing-library/user-event` ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá clicks, typing simulate ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
- **No Implementation Details:** Internal state ‡¶¨‡¶æ structure test ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡ßá user-facing output test ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
- **Accessible Queries:** Accessibility-focused queries (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® `getByRole`) encourage ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§

**Example:**
```jsx
import { render, screen, fireEvent } from '@testing-library/react';
import MyComponent from './MyComponent';

test('button toggles text', () => {
  render(<MyComponent />);
  expect(screen.getByText('Off')).toBeInTheDocument();
  fireEvent.click(screen.getByRole('button'));
  expect(screen.getByText('On')).toBeInTheDocument();
});
```

**Why Popular:**
- **User-Centric:** Tests user-‡¶è‡¶∞ perspective ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º, ‡¶Ø‡¶æ real-world scenarios reflect ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
- **Simple API:** Intuitive queries ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç minimal setup‡•§
- **Encourages Best Practices:** Implementation details avoid ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá robust tests ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ñ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
- **Compatibility:** Jest, TypeScript, ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç modern React (hooks) ‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
- **Community Support:** Wide adoption ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç active community‡•§

**Use case:** React Testing Library ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶ø user behavior test ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç maintainable test suites ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ñ‡¶§‡ßá‡•§



### _#57._ üü£ **What are some best practices for writing clean React code?**

Clean React code ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ best practices:

1. **Use Functional Components and Hooks:**
   - Modern React-‡¶è functional components ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç hooks (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® `useState`, `useEffect`) ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
   - Class components ‡¶è‡¶°‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã, ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ hooks simpler ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç less boilerplate‡•§
   ```jsx
   const Counter = () => {
     const [count, setCount] = useState(0);
     return <button onClick={() => setCount(count + 1)}>{count}</button>;
   };
   ```

2. **Keep Components Small and Focused:**
   - Single responsibility principle follow ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
   - Large components-‡¶ï‡ßá smaller, reusable components-‡¶è ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶ó ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
   ```jsx
   const UserCard = ({ user }) => (
     <div>
       <UserName name={user.name} />
       <UserDetails details={user.details} />
     </div>
   );
   ```

3. **Use Descriptive Naming:**
   - Components, variables, ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç functions-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶Æ meaningful ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
   - Example: `Button` ‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡ßá `SubmitButton` ‡¶¨‡¶æ `ToggleSwitch`‡•§

4. **Avoid Prop Drilling:**
   - Context API ‡¶¨‡¶æ state management libraries (Redux, Zustand) ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
   ```jsx
   const ThemeContext = createContext();
   const App = () => (
     <ThemeContext.Provider value="dark">
       <Child />
     </ThemeContext.Provider>
   );
   ```

5. **Optimize Performance:**
   - `React.memo`, `useMemo`, `useCallback` ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá unnecessary re-renders prevent ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
   - Lists-‡¶è unique `key` prop ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
   ```jsx
   const MemoizedComponent = React.memo(({ value }) => <div>{value}</div>);
   ```

6. **Use TypeScript for Type Safety:**
   - Props ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç state-‡¶è‡¶∞ types define ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
   ```jsx
   interface Props {
     name: string;
   }
   const MyComponent: React.FC<Props> = ({ name }) => <div>{name}</div>;
   ```

7. **Follow Consistent Folder Structure:**
   - Components, hooks, utils, ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç tests-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø organized folders‡•§
   - Example: `src/components/`, `src/hooks/`, `src/__tests__/`.

8. **Write Reusable and DRY Code:**
   - Custom hooks ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá logic reuse ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
   - Common UI patterns (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® buttons, modals) component libraries ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
   ```jsx
   const useToggle = () => {
     const [isOn, setIsOn] = useState(false);
     return [isOn, () => setIsOn(!isOn)];
   };
   ```

9. **Handle Errors Gracefully:**
   - Error boundaries ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
   - API errors ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç form validation handle ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
   ```jsx
   class ErrorBoundary extends React.Component {
     state = { hasError: false };
     static getDerivedStateFromError() { return { hasError: true }; }
     render() { return this.state.hasError ? <h1>Error</h1> : this.props.children; }
   }
   ```

10. **Write Tests:**
    - React Testing Library ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá unit ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç integration tests ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
    - Test coverage maintain ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§

11. **Use ESLint and Prettier:**
    - Consistent code style enforce ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ESLint ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç Prettier ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶®‡•§
    - Example: `eslint-plugin-react`, `eslint-plugin-react-hooks`‡•§

**Use case:** Clean code maintainability, scalability, ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç collaboration ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶®‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç technical debt ‡¶ï‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§


‚úÖ 9. Miscellaneous
### _#58._ üü£ **What is React Portals and why is it used?**

React Portals ‡¶π‡¶≤‡ßã React-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø feature ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø component-‡¶è‡¶∞ DOM tree-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã DOM node-‡¶è child components render ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶Ø‡¶º, ‡¶Ø‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶ì component hierarchy-‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø parent-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡¶ß‡ßÄ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá‡•§ ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶æ `ReactDOM.createPortal` API ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá implement ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§

**How it works:**
- `createPortal` ‡¶¶‡ßÅ‡¶ü‡¶ø argument ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶Ø‡¶º: JSX (child) ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç DOM node (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá render ‡¶π‡¶¨‡ßá)‡•§
- Portals event bubbling ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç React context maintain ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§

**Example:**
```jsx
import { createPortal } from 'react-dom';

const Modal = ({ children }) => {
  return createPortal(
    <div className="modal">{children}</div>,
    document.getElementById('modal-root') // DOM node outside root
  );
};

const App = () => (
  <div>
    <Modal>Modal Content</Modal>
  </div>
);
```

**Why used:**
- **Modals/Overlays:** Modals, popups, ‡¶¨‡¶æ tooltips DOM-‡¶è‡¶∞ root-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶∞‡ßá render ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá‡•§
- **Z-Index Issues:** CSS stacking issues ‡¶è‡¶°‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá‡•§
- **Third-Party Integration:** External DOM nodes-‡¶è render ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá‡•§
- **Accessibility:** Event bubbling maintain ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá accessible components ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá‡•§

**Use case:** Portals ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶ø modals, dialogs, ‡¶¨‡¶æ global UI elements render ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶æ main DOM tree-‡¶è‡¶∞ constraints ‡¶è‡¶°‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§



### _#59._ üü£ **What is the difference between SSR, CSR, and SSG in context of React (Next.js)?**

| **Aspect**           | **CSR (Client-Side Rendering)** | **SSR (Server-Side Rendering)** | **SSG (Static Site Generation)** |
|----------------------|--------------------------------|--------------------------------|----------------------------------|
| **Definition**       | Browser-‡¶è JavaScript ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá UI render ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§ | Server-‡¶è HTML generate ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç browser-‡¶è ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§ | Build time-‡¶è static HTML generate ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§ |
| **How it works**     | Initial blank HTML ‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶° ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º, ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶™‡¶∞ JS UI render ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§ | Server ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø request-‡¶è HTML ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§ | Pages build time-‡¶è pre-render ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§ |
| **Example in Next.js** | Default React behavior (`create-react-app`)‡•§ | `getServerSideProps` ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§ | `getStaticProps` ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§ |
| **Performance**      | Initial load slower, client-side heavy‡•§ | Faster initial load, server-side heavy‡•§ | Fastest initial load, minimal server load‡•§ |
| **SEO**              | Poor, ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ initial HTML empty‡•§ | Good, ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ server HTML ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§ | Excellent, ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ static HTML pre-rendered‡•§ |
| **Use Case**         | Dynamic apps ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá SEO priority ‡¶®‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§ | Dynamic data, frequent updates‡•§ | Static content (blogs, docs)‡•§ |

**Example (Next.js):**
```jsx
// SSR (getServerSideProps)
export async function getServerSideProps() {
  const data = await fetchData();
  return { props: { data } };
}

// SSG (getStaticProps)
export async function getStaticProps() {
  const data = await fetchData();
  return { props: { data } };
}
```

**Use case:** CSR simple SPAs-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø, SSR dynamic data ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç SEO-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø, SSG static content ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç fast performance-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø‡•§



### _#60._ üü£ **What is hydration in React?**

Hydration ‡¶π‡¶≤‡ßã React-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø process ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá server-side rendered (SSR) ‡¶¨‡¶æ static site generated (SSG) HTML-‡¶ï‡ßá client-‡¶è interactive ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶§‡ßã‡¶≤‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§ Next.js-‡¶è ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶æ common‡•§

**How it works:**
- Server HTML generate ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá browser-‡¶è ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
- Client-‡¶è React JavaScript ‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶° ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç HTML-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá event listeners attach ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
- Hydration-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞ component fully interactive ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§

**Example (Next.js):**
```jsx
// pages/index.jsx
export async function getServerSideProps() {
  return { props: { message: 'Hello' } };
}

const Home = ({ message }) => <div>{message}</div>;

export default Home;
// Server: Renders HTML with "Hello"
// Client: Hydrates HTML to make it interactive
```

**Key Points:**
- Hydration performance-critical, ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶æ client-side JS execution ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
- Next.js-‡¶è partial hydration (React 18) performance ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶®‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§

**Use case:** Hydration ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶ø SSR/SSG apps-‡¶è initial HTML-‡¶ï‡ßá interactive ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá‡•§



### _#61._ üü£ **What is the purpose of keys in rendering a list?**

`key` prop ‡¶π‡¶≤‡ßã React-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø special attribute ‡¶Ø‡¶æ list rendering-‡¶è elements uniquely identify ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§ ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶æ reconciliation process optimize ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§

**Purpose:**
- **Efficient Updates:** React `key` ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá list items-‡¶è‡¶∞ changes (add, remove, reorder) track ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§
- **Prevent Re-renders:** Correct keys unchanged items-‡¶è‡¶∞ re-rendering ‡¶è‡¶°‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
- **Maintain State:** List items-‡¶è‡¶∞ state (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® input values) preserve ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§

**Example:**
```jsx
const List = ({ items }) => (
  <ul>
    {items.map((item) => (
      <li key={item.id}>{item.name}</li> // Unique key
    ))}
  </ul>
);
```

**Rules:**
- `key` unique ‡¶π‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶π‡¶¨‡ßá sibling elements-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá‡•§
- Index ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶°‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶â‡¶ö‡¶ø‡¶§, ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ list order change ‡¶π‡¶≤‡ßá issues ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
- Stable IDs (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® database IDs) best‡•§

**Use case:** `key` ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶ø lists efficiently render ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç performance issues ‡¶è‡¶°‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá‡•§



### _#62._ üü£ **What is the difference between Fragment and div in React?**

| **Aspect**            | **Fragment**                                              | **div**                                                  |
|-----------------------|----------------------------------------------------------|---------------------------------------------------------|
| **Definition**        | React-‡¶è‡¶∞ virtual wrapper ‡¶Ø‡¶æ DOM-‡¶è extra node ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶æ‡•§ | HTML element ‡¶Ø‡¶æ DOM-‡¶è actual `<div>` tag ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§       |
| **Syntax**            | `<Fragment>` ‡¶¨‡¶æ shorthand `<>...</>`                    | `<div>...</div>`                                       |
| **DOM Impact**        | No extra DOM node, cleaner markup‡•§                       | Adds `<div>` to DOM, ‡¶Ø‡¶æ unnecessary nesting ‡¶∏‡ßÉ‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§ |
| **Use Case**          | Multiple children return ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá, styling ‡¶¶‡¶∞‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶á‡•§        | Styling ‡¶¨‡¶æ layout-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø actual DOM element ‡¶¶‡¶∞‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡•§     |
| **Example**           | `<><h1>Title</h1><p>Text</p></>`                       | `<div><h1>Title</h1><p>Text</p></div>`                |

**Fragment Example:**
```jsx
const MyComponent = () => (
  <>
    <h1>Title</h1>
    <p>Text</p>
  </>
);
```

**div Example:**
```jsx
const MyComponent = () => (
  <div>
    <h1>Title</h1>
    <p>Text</p>
  </div>
);
```

**Key Points:**
- Fragments CSS ‡¶¨‡¶æ layout issues ‡¶è‡¶°‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡•§
- `<Fragment>` key prop support ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá (list rendering-‡¶è)‡•§
- `div` ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶≤‡ßá unnecessary DOM nodes ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶°‡¶º‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§

**Use case:** Fragments ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶ø clean DOM structure ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç unnecessary markup ‡¶è‡¶°‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá; `div` styling ‡¶¨‡¶æ structural needs-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø‡•§



# ‚ú® JavaScript based interview questions

_#08._ You have a API that fetches a user's details, but it sometimes takes a long time to respond. You need to show a loading spinner waiting for the API response and hide it once the data is fetched. How would you implement this?

_#14._ How would you handle a situation where two APIs depend on each other. for example, imagine you're building a social media app, The first API fetches for user content like user name, host content etc. and the second API fetches the likes and comments for that post. now what if the first API fails, how would you ensure the second API only runs if the first one is successful?

# ‚ú® React based interview questions

_#02._ What are the rules of `hooks` in react?
_Ans:_ There are 3 rules of `hooks`

1. **Top-Level Only:** use `hooks` at the top level of your `functional components`. not inside `loops`, `conditions`, or `nested functions`.
2. **React Functions Only:** call `hooks` only from react `functional components`, or `custom hooks`. not from regular javascript functions.
3. **No Conditions:** call hooks unconditionally at the top level without any `if-else` statements or conditions.

_#05._ You have a table with hundreds of rows. How can you efficiently handle a click event on every row without adding an event listener to each row?
_/ event delegation, event bubbling /_

_#07._ You need to implement an infinite scrolling feature in a react application where more data loads as the user scrolls down. How would you achieve this?

_#08._ You need to render a list of 10,000 items in the react application, but rendering all items at once causes performance issues. How would you optimize this? _/ virtualization /_

_#10._ You have a search bar that fetches from an API. The problem is that API is called every time the user types a letter which overloads the server with unnecessary request. How would you optimize this?

_#11._ You have a login page where the user loges in successfully. But as soon as user refreshes the page, they get logged out. Why does this happen and how would you fix it?

_#15._ Imagine you're building a social media platform like facebook. Now you want to let users switch between newest first and oldest first comments using a dropdown. How would you implement this features?

_#16._ Imagine you're building a web page that shows data from an API. If the API fails due to bad internet or server error. How will you handle it?

_#17._ Imagine you're building a gmail like app. when a user delete an email instead of removing it instantly you app should show a small message like "Message will delete in 5s, Undo?" this message should stay visible for 5 seconds and giving the user a chance to cancel. how would you implement this undo delete feature in your code?

_#18._ Imagine you're building a YouTube style app, when a user uploads a video, you need to show a real time upload progress like 0% to 100%. How would you implement this live progress bar UI plus backend upload logic in react?

_#19._ You have a submit button in your form. But when the user clicks multiple times quickly, your API gets called again and again. How can you prevent multiple API calls on repeated button clicks in react?

_Ans:_ To solve this, I'll follow these steps.

- **step 1:** use a loading state like isSubmitting. to track if the API call is already in progress, while it's true disable the button, so the user can't click again.
- **step 2:** we can also use use ref to store a flag that prevents repeated submission without rerendering.
- **step 3:** for more advanced control. apply a debounce method to delay the function call. If clicks happen rapidly.
